DISCHARGE DIAGNOSES

Procedures/Interventions/Operations:
None
Reason for hospitalization (as dictated at the time of admission)
HPI altered mental status
Kimberly K Brasher is a 49 y.o. female with PMH of closed left intertrochanteric fracture s/p ORIF [DOB-11],
chronic iron-deficiency anemia, gastric bypass surgery, migraine headaches who was brought to the ED after
being found unresponsive by her daughter at home. Daughter reports that patient received Norco 5.0 mg x 20
tabs on 3/7. She had a follow up with her orthopedic surgeon yesterday (3/9) and received an additional 28
tablets of Norco 7.5 mg. Daughter believes that patient took all of these since getting her prescription filled.
 Per ED documentation patient was awake and alert with GCS 15 on arrival but slow to respond with slurred
Thu Sep 21, 2023 12:12 PM

Discharge Summary - Discharge Summary (continued)
Discharge Summary by Vasser-Smith, Montubua, MD at 03/12/23 1137 (continued)
speech. She did not require Narcan.
Vitals on arrival notable for pulse 155. Notable labs: Hemoglobin 7.5, INR 2.0, AST 48, TSH 5.80 with normal
free T4, acetaminophen level 41. CT head and CT cervical spine negative for acute process. X-ray of the left
hip showed intact hardware. Chest x-ray was negative. ED physician discussed case with poison control and
patient was started on NAC protocol in addition to Protonix 40 mg and 1 L normal saline bolus. Hospitalist
service was contacted for admission.
Hospital Course:
Kimberly K BrasherN was admitted to the ICU in guarded condition. She was started on NAC
protocol. Her AST returned to normal levels and her acetaminophen level was undetectable by the next
morning. Her INR fell from 2.0 down to 1.4, hemoglobin remains stable at her baseline of
approximately 7-7.5. I do recommend she follow-up with Hematology with her history of iron deficient
anemia. Patient had completed her NAC, and given all numbers returned to normal range, it was
discontinued
Patient adamantly denies any form of self-harm, appears to be quite embarrassed for the events that
happened. She is unsure how she became so confused and overdosed on the medication. She is
eager to be able to get back home, understands she will not have opiates to help control her pain, and
this does bring her some anxiety. Chart review shows previous visits to Psychiatry where notes do not
reveal any prior SI/HI. Recommendation is to follow-up outpatient psychiatry. Patient was offered
Ultram at discharge but she declined.
PT did recommend inpatient rehab however the patient is adamant that she does not want facility level
rehab and will follow-up as outpatient with her previous order for PT.
Hypokalemia was noted on the morning of 3/11. Potassium 2.8. Patient was given oral and IV
replacement. On the day of discharge potassium has normalized at 3.8.
Physical Exam:
GENERAL: Frail appearing white female in no acute distress.
CHEST: Clear to auscultation bilaterally without wheezes, stridor, crackles. Adequate inspiratory effort and air
flow. No accessory muscle use with breathing.
CARDIAC: Regular S1-S2. No murmur, rub, or gallop. No JVD, cyanosis, or leg edema.
ABDOMEN: Bowel sounds are audible. Soft, nontender, nondistended. No hepatosplenomegaly.
MUSCULOSKELETAL: S/p left hip ORIF, incision c/d/i
SKIN: Warm and dry. No rashes.
NEUROLOGIC: Awake and alert speech is clear quite conversant. 5/5 strength in bilateral upper and lower
extremities. Cranial nerves 2-12 are intact. No gross sensory deficits.
PSYCHIATRIC: Alert and oriented x3. Pleasant mood and affect.
Condition upon Discharge: Improved
Disposition: Home with outpatient PT
Instructions for follow up care:

Chief Complaint
Patient presents with •Drug Overdose
HPI
Kimberly K Brasher is a 49 y.o. female who presents with last known well of 8:00 p.m. last night. She had left
hip surgery 2 weeks ago. She was prescribed new prescription of Norco yesterday. Her daughter filled it. At
2:30 a.m. this morning daughter noticed that she was confused thinking that she was working in nursing home.
She then fell in her bedroom. Patient is confused and altered. Disoriented answers appropriate age and
name. Confabulates story though from patient. She denies pain anywhere other than her left hip. Patient
denies any suicide ideation or self-harm ideation. She states she is not take anything to harm herself. Patient
states that she thinks this is due to the medication. Daughter notes that her recent Norco bottles are
completely emptying they were filled yesterday. She is also prescribed Flexeril and Xarelto to prevent blood
clots. Denies alcohol or illicit drugs. Daughter states no concern for self-harm.
Estimate she took 28 tablets of norco 7.5-325 between 8pm and 2:30am: That is 9100mg tylenol, 150mg/kg =
8550mg is toxic dose. Poison control notified

being found unresponsive by her daughter at home. Daughter reports that patient received Norco 5.0 mg x 20
tabs on 3/7. She had a follow up with her orthopedic surgeon yesterday (3/9) and received an additional 28
tablets of Norco 7.5 mg. Daughter believes that patient took all of these since getting her prescription filled.

speech. She did not require Narcan.

investigation of non-bacterial or non-infectious causes of patient clinical status. Repeat low

PMD: No primary care provider on file.
Reason for hospitalization
Kimberly K Brasher is a 49 y.o. female with PMH of closed left intertrochanteric fracture s/p ORIF [DOB-96],
chronic iron-deficiency anemia, gastric bypass surgery, migraine headaches who was brought to the ED after
being found unresponsive by her daughter at home. Daughter reports that patient received Norco 5.0 mg x 20
tabs on 3/7. She had a follow up with her orthopedic surgeon yesterday (3/9) and received an additional 28
tablets of Norco 7.5 mg. Daughter believes that patient took all of these since getting her prescription filled.
 Per ED documentation patient was awake and alert with GCS 15 on arrival but slow to respond with slurred
speech. She did not require Narcan.
Vitals on arrival notable for pulse 155. Notable labs: Hemoglobin 7.5, INR 2.0, AST 48, TSH 5.80 with normal
free T4, acetaminophen level 41. CT head and CT cervical spine negative for acute process. X-ray of the left
hip showed intact hardware. Chest x-ray was negative. ED physician discussed case with poison control and
patient was started on NAC protocol in addition to Protonix 40 mg and 1 L normal saline bolus. Hospitalist
service was contacted for admission.
Hospital course
Patient was admitted to the ICU in guarded condition. She was started on NAC protocol. Her AST
returned to normal levels and her acetaminophen level was undetectable by the next morning. Her INR
fell from 2.0 down to 1.4, hemoglobin remains stable at her baseline of approximately 7-7.5. I do
recommend she follow-up with Hematology with her history of iron deficient anemia. Patient had
completed her NAC, and given all numbers returned to normal range, it was discontinued
Patient adamantly denies any form of self-harm, appears to be quite embarrassed for the events that
happened. She is unsure how she became so confused and overdosed on the medication. She is
eager to be able to get back home, understands she will not have opiates to help control her pain, and
this does bring her some anxiety. Chart review shows previous visits to Psychiatry where notes do not
reveal any prior SI/HI. Recommendation is to follow-up outpatient psychiatry.
Hypokalemia was noted on the morning of 3/11. Potassium 2.8. Patient was given oral and IV

Antibiotics are strongly discouraged.
Antibiotic INITIATION should not be withheld if highly suspicious for sepsis.
Recommend repeat PCT if antibiotics not given and not improved in 6-12 hours. ==================== Procalcitonin Normals -- — — DHND
Result:
GENERAL COMMENTS Antibiotic initiation should not be withheld for patients with sepsis or
pneumonia with radiographic evidence of infiltrates. A low procalcitonin should prompt the
investigation of non-bacterial or non-infectious causes of patient clinical status. Repeat low
 or declining procalcitonin (>80% from peak) may indicate an opportunity for antibiotic
de-escalation or discontinuation. Low procalcitonin levels in the presence of acute bronchitis,
 COPD exacerbations, and other related conditions generally indicates the absence of clinically
 significant bacterial infections. Please refer to the procalcitonin guidance document on DWeb
 under Quick Links - Antimicrobial Stewardship for additional information.
